  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_96ad6088-deb2-4353-ba3b-d1ff6de4cff4'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer856449014404225038">The setting is East Texas, where Peggy, a young nurse, works at an institution for the criminally insane. After her husband Danny is mysteriously killed in a car accident, she convinces herself that it was murder… and she knows the murderer by name… Jasper Johnson. When she gets notice from Marbelle Johnson, Jasper’s mother, requesting an impromptu meeting, she discovers t</span>
  <span id="freeText856449014404225038" style="display:none">The setting is East Texas, where Peggy, a young nurse, works at an institution for the criminally insane. After her husband Danny is mysteriously killed in a car accident, she convinces herself that it was murder… and she knows the murderer by name… Jasper Johnson. When she gets notice from Marbelle Johnson, Jasper’s mother, requesting an impromptu meeting, she discovers that the filthy rich oil baroness believes Danny to have been the bastard child of her deceased husband, Charles Johnson. <br /> <br />Peggy, irreparably damaged from childhood by religious fanaticism, reluctantly agrees to exhume Danny’s body. Reeling with doubt, all the while fearing betrayal by the Johnsons, she finds herself bordering on insanity. <br /> <br />Shackled in darkness, Peggy throws herself into her work only to find herself face to face with a blonde haired, blue eyed schizophrenic in a straitjacket. Quite by circumstance she discovers that this patient, Morgan Dubois, who as a child was found burrowed in the ground in the Piney Wood Thicket, has a link not only to her late husband, but also to the aberrations of her mind. <br /> <br />As secrets are revealed and it becomes apparent that something or someone wants to silence their tongues, Peggy is forced to seek refuge with the Johnsons. Together, as death finds them, one by one, they set upon a perilous journey in search of truth. Deep in the heart of the Piney Wood Thicket, they stumble upon Cypress Creek and discover an existence older than time itself. Peggy, caught in a maelstrom of emotions, torn between two worlds, finds herself in a desperate battle, not only for her life, but for that of all of mankind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="856449014404225038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2120655595" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120655595" />
    <a title="Lydia Peever" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2978315-lydia-peever"><img alt="Lydia Peever" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486563275p2/2978315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120655595?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lydia Peever" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lydia Peever" href="/user/show/2978315-lydia-peever">Lydia Peever</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2978315-lydia-peever?shelf=paid-reviews">paid-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120655595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13120769664514099965">Written in the first person, “The Taking of Peggy Martin” certainly snags attention as author Karen Glista drags you fast through the deep south. We meet the widowed Peggy, who turns out to be a well educated and God-fearing nurse. The more we learn about her, the darker she gets. From sleeplessness to self-harm, her psyche is haunted as they come. It is easy to feel for her being wracked with insomnia and enchanted by her stories of youth--her grandmother, the townsfolk and church--but knowing </span>
  <span id="freeText13120769664514099965" style="display:none">Written in the first person, “The Taking of Peggy Martin” certainly snags attention as author Karen Glista drags you fast through the deep south. We meet the widowed Peggy, who turns out to be a well educated and God-fearing nurse. The more we learn about her, the darker she gets. From sleeplessness to self-harm, her psyche is haunted as they come. It is easy to feel for her being wracked with insomnia and enchanted by her stories of youth--her grandmother, the townsfolk and church--but knowing she's hounded by the death of her husband. Soon the cracks start to show as her waking nightmares become all too real. <br /><br />After a horrific incident at work in the halls of the mental asylum worms into her sleepless nights, we lose sight of the line between nurse and patient. She's in need of help and unable to ask as trying to keep her life together takes too much time and energy. Then, she comes face to face with Morgan. A feral young man who is rumoured to be mute and wild after living alone in the Piney Wood Thicket following the mysterious disappearance of his entire family. <br /><br />It's doubly unnerving to read as we see through Peggy’s eyes and are privy to her unravelling thoughts, but unnerving in the best way. Then, everything gets unnaturally dark, and the forces behind her husband’s death and Morgan’s past entwine. This takes us into the bulk of the book where the story delves deep into horror and science fiction; something one would barely expect from the first quarter which reads like a regency drama set in the 50s. <br /><br />So much purple prose is woven by Glista that some readers may need tinted glasses to get by. At times it works, being thrust deep into the heart of Texas, but some lines are far too flowery even for the sweetest rose. It persists, wonderfully, through the most vile scenes of gore and inhumanity that Peggy witnesses so the very colourful writing serves to break tension during rape, cannibalism, decapitations, eviscerations and buckets of gore. This may not be everyone’s cup of tea, but it was a welcome and refreshing mix. It’s really more of a tall glass of iced tea on a hot stormy afternoon… with a human eyeball bobbing around under the cubes and lemon wedge. There are so many colloquialisms and regional manners of speaking it would take some research by those not familiar with Texas to see if they are all actual slang and in common usage. Those who baulk at dialect being written out at every turn would find this trying, though Glista can thank the first quarter of her work for truly setting a tone and creating a space with rules so the reader is kind of tied to the horse as it were. And boy, can that horse jump.<br /><br />The novel is listed as supernatural first and foremost then mystery, though considering the amount of gore and the nature of Peggy’s relationship with the other inhabitants of the Thicket, I’d have to stick it right into horror if not bizarro science-fiction. As a fan of the former I could rate this at three stars easily if not four for the latter. Fans of bizarro horror cult hit “The Gospel of Bucky Dennis: A Southern Gothic Horror Hymn” by J. R. Parks would adore this, and perhaps those who watched the current mini-series gem “Jordskott” but wanted it to be a little more racy and action-packed will get a lot out of “The Taking of Peggy Martin”. The only place where this loses points is having so much packed into the story that the pace varies wildly from a giddy trot to a breakneck race to get it all in--and the flowery terms alongside overused phrases. Where it wins, however, kept me sucked into the insane steeplechase this little widow finds herself on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13120769664514099965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2132249492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2132249492" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70404846-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2132249492?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/70404846-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2132249492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3670509810117095334">In reading The Taking of Peggy Martin by Karen Glista, I found it to be somewhat confusing, but also an interesting book. The main character is Peggy Martin herself. Peggy is a tortured individual, dealing with a host of psychological and emotional traumas. Prior to the opening of the book, her husband, was killed suddenly in a car accident. This starts Peggy on a path that winds into a mental landscape of depression, self-harm, paranoia, hallucinations, and delusion. Yet, Peggy is also the hero</span>
  <span id="freeText3670509810117095334" style="display:none">In reading The Taking of Peggy Martin by Karen Glista, I found it to be somewhat confusing, but also an interesting book. The main character is Peggy Martin herself. Peggy is a tortured individual, dealing with a host of psychological and emotional traumas. Prior to the opening of the book, her husband, was killed suddenly in a car accident. This starts Peggy on a path that winds into a mental landscape of depression, self-harm, paranoia, hallucinations, and delusion. Yet, Peggy is also the heroine of the story, as she seeks meaning in a world that seems bent on causing her pain. 	<br /><br />The story follows Peggy as she works to break free of her life circumstances and social surroundings. Of course, she is working to move past her traumas and resulting mental health issues. But also, the book is set in East Texas in the 1950s. As most know, that place and time period is not known for culture, inclusion, or progressive views. Peggy earnestly does not want to be viewed as a hick from Texas. Peggy works as a psychiatric nurse in a state mental institution, Rusk State Hospital. There she meets Morgan Dubois, a new inmate. He starts her on the path to exploring herself, her secrets, her past, her husband's death, and her future. Along this path, the last two central characters soon emerge, a mother-son team of Marbelle and Jasper Johnson. Much of the action of the story begins once Peggy meets these two. This begins her journey, which is filled with seemingly divine assistance, mental and physical tribulations, a great struggle against powers beyond comprehension, and a journey to a drastically altered life and new view of the world.<br /><br />This book has an M. Night Shyamalan-worthy twist, which I do not want to say too much about, as I do not want to reveal any potential spoilers. Towards the end of the book, there are also hints that the story is even more complex than I initially suspected and understood. So, I took a look back at a few different events and I think I may be right. As you read, keep good track of Peggy Martin, Morgan Dubois, Marbelle and Jasper Johnson. I would especially pay close attention to the character of Morgan Dubois as I believe he is even more complex than he initially seems. I will admit, my views and conclusions feel based on some ambiguous endings and plot points, so it may be up for discussion. On the one hand, I feel frustrated that things are ambiguous and I am left with uncertain interpretations. But I also look forward to having friends and family read this book so I can get their take on it. <br /><br />While this book is very interesting, I will admit that I struggled with the plot development and writing style. The story's beginning was rough, it felt entangled with the sudden introduction of numerous characters, and a rush to fill in some of Peggy's backstory. The action comes then comes in fits and starts, and is sometimes intensely graphic. At times, the writing seemed pretentious, with many words we do not use in typical conversation. For example, the terms phlegmatic, hypnagogia, whilom, and acknowledged consciousness are all on the very first page. Sometimes I had to use an internet search to make sure I understood the meanings. The text also included nearly constant internal monologue and dialogue. For example, there were around a half-dozen named characters in the first chapter alone that would interact and the dialogue was not clearly presented. It made it very hard to tell who was talking. It also took me a bit of time to figure out when the story was set and I wish the author would have clearly presented that information to the reader as it helps to form a visual picture of the action.<br /><br />Looking past writing style, overall, this was also a slow building story, so it took me a while to get engaged, but once the story did get going, it was a wild ride. The story really takes off and ends with a satisfying, albeit it, twisty conclusion. A final note, this book is definitely intended for mature readers, as it contains graphic depictions of violence, including sexual assault, severe mental illness, and death. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3670509810117095334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2186889012" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2186889012" />
    <a title="Novel Addiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73909712-novel-addiction"><img alt="Novel Addiction" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/images/nophoto/user/c_111x148.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2186889012?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Novel Addiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Novel Addiction" href="/user/show/73909712-novel-addiction">Novel Addiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2186889012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1126180949536068793">Peggy Martin is a widow living alone in her grandmother’s home in East Texas, a country setting where everyone knows everyone. Peggy is a psychiatric nurse at a place for the “criminally insane” and she always has the willies about her workplace as horrific incidents have happened there to her colleagues where one woman was violently, bloodily violated by one of the patients permanently confined there. Peggy is a self-made woman who defied her fellow residents by going back to school in earning </span>
  <span id="freeText1126180949536068793" style="display:none">Peggy Martin is a widow living alone in her grandmother’s home in East Texas, a country setting where everyone knows everyone. Peggy is a psychiatric nurse at a place for the “criminally insane” and she always has the willies about her workplace as horrific incidents have happened there to her colleagues where one woman was violently, bloodily violated by one of the patients permanently confined there. Peggy is a self-made woman who defied her fellow residents by going back to school in earning her degree which is why she has this job in the first place. Peggy comes off to the reader of this book as a God-fearing, mentally restless, and devoted to her dead husband woman who can’t stop thinking of her dead grandmother’s heartfelt maternal ways and is always quoting passages from the Holy Bible to get through her days.<br /><br />Now it just so happens that Peggy comes in contact with a patient at her workplace by the name of Morgan who seems to be not of this world according to Peggy’s observations. His body looks like it has spikes and his eyes seem to change colors and can look reptilian at times. Peggy discovers he’s one of the members of a remote forest-dwelling family of East Texas that has gone missing with this particular man having been found by authorities with his head burrowed in the ground and behaving in an animalistic way. Peggy knows this is the same location where her husband and a family friend went hunting before his car accident that took his life.<br /><br />Soon Peggy’s world is turned into a nightmare when she pries further and further into Morgan’s personal life, finding peculiar odds and ends about his speech and what he talks about. Peggy and a group of family acquaintances are being attacked by creatures not of this world who are extremely inhumane and sadistic with no mercy in their killings. Peggy’s husband’s body turns up missing from his coffin and the body in his place also exhibits the same spikes she saw on Morgan’s body. The world seems to be ending when she and a few others come in contact with demonic creatures who Peggy swears are agents from hell unleashed to bring destruction upon all mankind and that sooner or later the help of the military will be needed to fend them off and put an end to their grotesque existence.<br /><br />This book is part horror, part comedy, and part fantasy. It’s a mixture of those three elements and even though the violence and gore are disturbing, you can always chuckle at the sense of humor that Glista has in her way of writing this novel. I found her Bible passages inclusion mixed in with the Redneck vernacular of the characters to be quite hilarious because forgive me if I am being facetious, it’s just so reminiscent of comedies that air on TV. I am sure you will appreciate that when you are reading this book because it counters the extreme graphic descriptions of its horrors and spooks. I strongly urge you to buy this book today in time for Halloween tomorrow as you will genuinely become scared of the “trees” (the Silent Hill-esque creatures of this book). Be sure to be prepared for the great twist that comes near the end! Enjoy!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1126180949536068793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2125395278" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2125395278" />
    <a title="David Gunner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70680685-david-gunner"><img alt="David Gunner" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2125395278?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Gunner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Gunner" href="/user/show/70680685-david-gunner">David Gunner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2125395278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6987594098288971240">The Taking of Peggy Martin: Dark before Dawn<br/>After her husband’s death, Peggy Sue Martin somewhat just stumbles through life. She wakes up, makes coffee, goes to work then comes back home and grieves through the rest of the time. She is convinced that her job is her only saving grace. Peggy suffers misfortunes in life and at some point even thinks she may be going crazy. What she does not know is that her life is very close to changing forever. Up to this point, the biggest events in her life wer</span>
  <span id="freeText6987594098288971240" style="display:none">The Taking of Peggy Martin: Dark before Dawn<br />After her husband’s death, Peggy Sue Martin somewhat just stumbles through life. She wakes up, makes coffee, goes to work then comes back home and grieves through the rest of the time. She is convinced that her job is her only saving grace. Peggy suffers misfortunes in life and at some point even thinks she may be going crazy. What she does not know is that her life is very close to changing forever. Up to this point, the biggest events in her life were losing Grandmother Flossie and then Danny. More is yet to come. The fate that befalls East Texas begins and ends with Peggy. Little Peggy who is easily bypassed because she is sad and has dark circles under her eyes. Little Peggy, who sits awake alone all night. The path that Peggy is about to walk is scary but she has an unlikely partner.<br />When creatures invade the county, only a few know about the matter. These few are in danger from the said creatures. The same few embark on a mission to find out what they have planned. The result of their fury-filled curiosity is morbid. They have lost people they love in the fight but they still have each other in the end. Peggy has something in her possession that the Koit-Zue wants. The three of them might be on the run all their lives. One thing is for sure though, baby Belle will live it up.<br />“You’re getting hotter than a goat’s butt in a pepper patch” The book is colored with such language, which brings so much humor amidst all the tragedy. It is so authentically Southern in a way that a reader will appreciate. The ‘Texan drawl’ has a certain symphony to it. Something that makes it melodious to the ear. Peggy does not like it but reading in a Southern accent sure is fun. Karen Glista creates vivid images and scents in the Taking of Peggy Martin. She described things and smells down to the minutest detail. This quality is instrumental in transporting the reader to Cypress Creek. While reading through conversation between Morgan and Peggy one can almost smell the cocktail of pungent dead flesh mixed in with wanton sexual desire. The twists and turns in this story will keep the reader glued to the pages. It is an interesting sequence of events.<br />The characters are truly admirable. Peggy never completely loses her faith in God. She recites the Lord’s Prayer when the ‘sky trees’ surround her. She has incredible strength and enviable resilience. Marbelle Brookshire Johnson is another character who just impresses from the beginning to the end. She possesses such maternal concern for Peggy that the reader just has to love right from the get go. She makes a good companion for Peggy through the mucky trip. If the Koit-Zue do not get them, Morbella will be lucky to have her as a honorary grandmother.<br />If there are imperfections in this book, the reader will be easily blinded by the Southern tongue and impeccable imagery. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6987594098288971240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2151338095" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2151338095" />
    <a title="Alexander Pyles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10126874-alexander-pyles"><img alt="Alexander Pyles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572554482p2/10126874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2151338095?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexander Pyles" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexander Pyles" href="/user/show/10126874-alexander-pyles">Alexander Pyles</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2151338095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5650618880174679824">This was a story that I still have to scratch my head at, but then again, I’m not sure Karen Glista was sure where it was going either. The Taking of Peggy Martin begins as a murder mystery where nurse, Peggy Martin, a widow knows who murdered her husband in a bizarre car accident. She is contacted by the murderer’s mother for an impromptu meeting and it descends into the supernatural from there. Strong elements of horror and even science fiction creep into this work as well as more grisly actio</span>
  <span id="freeText5650618880174679824" style="display:none">This was a story that I still have to scratch my head at, but then again, I’m not sure Karen Glista was sure where it was going either. The Taking of Peggy Martin begins as a murder mystery where nurse, Peggy Martin, a widow knows who murdered her husband in a bizarre car accident. She is contacted by the murderer’s mother for an impromptu meeting and it descends into the supernatural from there. Strong elements of horror and even science fiction creep into this work as well as more grisly actions of rape and more murder. It is not a book for the faint of heart. <br /><br />Peggy herself struggles with insanity, which is ironic since she is a nurse at an insane asylum. She is a strong character on her own even with this instability but it does tend to take away from her character rather than add to it. With these mature themes, the book is obviously recommended for a mature or adult audience. Glista uses a lot of “purple” or verbose prose in her novel that can sometimes hide those more violent or disturbing images but they also place a wall in front of the reader if they are not familiar with such “ten dollar” words. While reading, I had to get out a dictionary which for a book like this, you do not want to do. <br /><br />The plot wasn’t boring by any means, but Glista tackles most of her character and world building in the first fourth of the novel and that can become a bit of a rush and makes the reader struggle to getting into the story. The pacing past this point settles down some and actual is a pleasant ride to some degree. Again, not sure what Glista was going for given the slang and verbose style but as a novel set in rural Texas it makes some sense. <br /><br />To the reader of thrillers, this may be a book for you. Even to readers of horror, this may be a book for you. Aside from those two groups, I’m unsure who else would want to pick this up but if you’re looking for a protagonist who is struggling with a deep internal conflict, The Taking of Peggy Martin is your best bet. Again a warning to readers that there are some intense pieces of gore and violence and is not recommended for the faint of heart.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5650618880174679824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2906216267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2906216267" />
    <a title="H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78657379-h"><img alt="H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520178267p2/78657379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2906216267?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="H" href="/user/show/78657379-h">H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906216267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13910311112732979331">The Taking of Peggy Martin is a thought-provoking read, this season. Karen Glista implicated depression, paranoia, hallucination and PTSD in a nifty manner, unique but slightly different. I had to read this book twice for me to visualise a poignant movie of it. It encapsulates culture, belongingness and exclusion, altogether. Highlighting that moving past tremors and plaguing memories of horrible life incidents to not only be difficult but also mentally infuriating. <br/><br/>It was a challenge, and Peggy</span>
  <span id="freeText13910311112732979331" style="display:none">The Taking of Peggy Martin is a thought-provoking read, this season. Karen Glista implicated depression, paranoia, hallucination and PTSD in a nifty manner, unique but slightly different. I had to read this book twice for me to visualise a poignant movie of it. It encapsulates culture, belongingness and exclusion, altogether. Highlighting that moving past tremors and plaguing memories of horrible life incidents to not only be difficult but also mentally infuriating. <br /><br />It was a challenge, and Peggy Martin the challenger!<br /><br />She works as a psychiatric nurse in a mental institution, meets a new inmate who later helps her find herself anew - Morgan Dubois. At his entry is another interesting beginning to the story, whereby she also meets Marbelle and Jasper Johnson, and discovers a fulfilling divine journey of hers, filled with mental assistance, scourge and a new perspective of the world. The writing style, character development and plot development are all excellent and fascinatingly complex. I had slight trouble at the start; reading and reading, confusion overwhelming me. There had been so many characters - I didn't know where the story would go. I do not have a problem with so many characters; albeit, when dialogue prompts mix-ups and perplexity, it becomes slow and somewhat paradoxical. <br /><br />The story having built on murder, mystery, and adult themes: Glista builds on a strong fitting character, built for ever challenging circumstances. Peggy Martin becomes inspiring through her impressively large, powerful, intense desire to push on through this anomaly, and her graphic past. I also enjoyed all the new expressions and unfamiliar words used throughout. Overall, I would say the beginning was rough, the middle becomes interesting, and the end holds a spectacular twist. I would definitely recommend this mature themed book for all murder, mystery and thriller lovers.<br /><br />4.4/5!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2869061953" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2869061953" />
    <a title="Kathleen Rohmer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62575250-kathleen-rohmer"><img alt="Kathleen Rohmer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520872691p2/62575250.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2869061953?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen Rohmer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen Rohmer" href="/user/show/62575250-kathleen-rohmer">Kathleen Rohmer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2869061953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14446516113263267722"> I was given a copy of this book for an honest review. However, I would give it an honest review regardless. This book has been the most engaging book I have read in a long time. The creative and clever descent into madness didn’t seem insane at all. I would call this the Twilight series of the 1950’s, but it really is a commentary on mental illness.<br/> I grew up in the Bible Belt of Texas and remember my father telling me that when he heard my granny whistling “The Old Rugged Cross” he knew to go </span>
  <span id="freeText14446516113263267722" style="display:none"> I was given a copy of this book for an honest review. However, I would give it an honest review regardless. This book has been the most engaging book I have read in a long time. The creative and clever descent into madness didn’t seem insane at all. I would call this the Twilight series of the 1950’s, but it really is a commentary on mental illness.<br /> I grew up in the Bible Belt of Texas and remember my father telling me that when he heard my granny whistling “The Old Rugged Cross” he knew to go and hide because someone’s butt was about to be whooped. It was black and white with no in-between. Many of the expressions used in this book are reminiscent of my dear old granny. The dialect is also accurate for East Texas. I loved the way the author incorporated local legend into the story as well. I remember as a child being scared to death of the legend of Boggy Creek. Even though I know it’s not real, I won’t spend the night at Boggy Creek.<br /> I found the details, expressions, actions, and beliefs to be consistent with those of the residents of East Texas in the 1950’s. The protagonist goes on such an exciting adventure, fraught with danger, intrigue, and genuine relationships, yet it is always optimistic and hopeful. Although it’s a romance, the author doesn’t get bogged down with sappy dialogue or sensitive details about intimate moments. The author did a magnificent job of building suspense in the beginning of the book and throwing a twist at the end that makes the reader question what just happened. People who do not enjoy this book may not understand what is written between the lines.<br /> I sincerely hope there is a sequel. I normally don’t like reading series, but in this case, I am curious about so many things. The author’s knowledge of nursing and psychology is an asset to her writing. I found this novel to be outstanding.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14446516113263267722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2398244208?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Black Swan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Black Swan" href="/user/show/82193466-black-swan">Black Swan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14904200634482949522">Peggy Martin is a god-fearing, lonely women, filling her days working a s a nurse in an Institution for the criminally insane, following the death of her beloved husband. Failing to sleep at night, and dealing with abhorrent patients during the day, she starts to feel like evil is stalking her every movement. Horrible, violent things have happened at the hospital, and it feels like something unspeakable is coming for her too. Is something dark really after Peggy, or is she simply crossing the ba</span>
  <span id="freeText14904200634482949522" style="display:none">Peggy Martin is a god-fearing, lonely women, filling her days working a s a nurse in an Institution for the criminally insane, following the death of her beloved husband. Failing to sleep at night, and dealing with abhorrent patients during the day, she starts to feel like evil is stalking her every movement. Horrible, violent things have happened at the hospital, and it feels like something unspeakable is coming for her too. Is something dark really after Peggy, or is she simply crossing the barrier from nurse to patient. I wondered for a long time whether 'The Taking of Peggy Martin' was the story of a vulnerable woman's journey into madness and despair, or if it was in fact the story of a woman who has awakened something ancient and diabolical that must be stopped. You will have to read Karin Glista's great novel to find out.<br /><br />The setting of 1950's America was a smart choice, as it fit really well with the underlying religious themes of the novel, which would have seemed out of place in a more contemporary backdrop. Furthermore, Glista's writing is filled with tension and atmosphere, plus her characters are extremely well-developed. I became very invested with Penny's fate, particularly as I couldn't predict what it could be. I simply couldn't stop reading.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14904200634482949522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2107589627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2107589627" />
    <a title="K.J. Simmill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37425428-k-j-simmill"><img alt="K.J. Simmill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502348866p2/37425428.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2107589627?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.J. Simmill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.J. Simmill" href="/user/show/37425428-k-j-simmill">K.J. Simmill</a>
      </span>

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2107589627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7442222656100694785">Peggy Martin wanted to make a difference, she wanted to care for people, give what she could. To those ends she became a nurse, and began to work at Rusk, a place that cared for the mentally unstable. But she had her own baggage. Her husband Danny was dead, murdered by his half-brother, or so she thought. But recent events caused her to question things she thought of as fact. Strange happenings and even stranger revelations cause her to question her own sanity as sleepless nights and disturbing </span>
  <span id="freeText7442222656100694785" style="display:none">Peggy Martin wanted to make a difference, she wanted to care for people, give what she could. To those ends she became a nurse, and began to work at Rusk, a place that cared for the mentally unstable. But she had her own baggage. Her husband Danny was dead, murdered by his half-brother, or so she thought. But recent events caused her to question things she thought of as fact. Strange happenings and even stranger revelations cause her to question her own sanity as sleepless nights and disturbing images haunt her every moment. She throws herself into work, but the things she discovers, even there, only raise more questions.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading this book. From the first page it is atmospheric. Amazingly written to show the suffering, doubts and questions. I'm not the biggest fan of first person perspective, but this is one of those books that change my mind. Through the author's style I was expertly given deep insight into Peggy's fragile psyche and was given a deep and personal understanding into all she faced. This is what first person perspective should be like. Even if this isn't a genre you'd normally read I highly recommend picking it up.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer7296823693739127250">'The Taking of Peggy Martin' by Karin Glista, is definitely a book that all horror genre fans should consider adding to their bookshelf. It is a super exciting novel, with a blistering pace, that will keep you gripped throughout the twists and turns. Glista manages to conjure an eerie atmosphere, and a feeling of paranoia. For a relatively new writer I was impressed by her ability to shape a scene complete with mood.<br/><br/>I don't want to give away too much of the plot, as I don't want to take away the</span>
  <span id="freeText7296823693739127250" style="display:none">'The Taking of Peggy Martin' by Karin Glista, is definitely a book that all horror genre fans should consider adding to their bookshelf. It is a super exciting novel, with a blistering pace, that will keep you gripped throughout the twists and turns. Glista manages to conjure an eerie atmosphere, and a feeling of paranoia. For a relatively new writer I was impressed by her ability to shape a scene complete with mood.<br /><br />I don't want to give away too much of the plot, as I don't want to take away the shock and surprise that I felt each time a new revelation was made. I will say that Peggy – a nurse at the aforementioned institution – finds herself descending into madness, after the sudden death of her husband. Then she meets Morgan, someone who may just have all the answers to her questions, but how much can you trust a criminally insane schizophrenic? And just how much can she trust herself? Can she escape the darkness that is stalking her and everyone she knows. Or will she too, find herself at the mercy of whatever lies in wait in the woods.<br /><br />A great little novel, well worth the price of fancy coffee, and will last so much longer.<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3187718733" />
    <a title="Jordan Brown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4737417-jordan-brown"><img alt="Jordan Brown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580152415p2/4737417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3187718733?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jordan Brown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jordan Brown" href="/user/show/4737417-jordan-brown">Jordan Brown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3187718733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2770883632554649809">I received a free digital copy of this novel in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>The Taking of Peggy Martin is a psychological thriller about a nurses’ descent into madness following the mysterious death of her husband. Author Karen Glista clearly wanted this book to have a strong sense of urgency but the pacing in the beginning was a little clunky for me. I think it would have helped the pacing if she had written it in present tense. One thing the novel does very well is create a strong sense of t</span>
  <span id="freeText2770883632554649809" style="display:none">I received a free digital copy of this novel in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />The Taking of Peggy Martin is a psychological thriller about a nurses’ descent into madness following the mysterious death of her husband. Author Karen Glista clearly wanted this book to have a strong sense of urgency but the pacing in the beginning was a little clunky for me. I think it would have helped the pacing if she had written it in present tense. One thing the novel does very well is create a strong sense of time and place. The way the characters talk puts you right in the story. <br /><br />The writing style can occasionally get bogged down in purple prose (prepare to see words like pusillanimous and stentorian used rather casually) but I rather liked the way it was infused with religious imagery to key us into Peggy’s state of mind. <br /><br />Plot wise, this swings for the fences and I appreciate that immensely, especially for something in this genre. If you can get through the exposition dense first quarter, there are some real surprises here. I wish half stars were allowed on Goodreads because this is definitely a solid 3.5. Overall I would recommend it if you're a fan of thrillers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2770883632554649809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2907728216858089437">The Taking of Peggy Martin by Karen Glista begins as a would be Southern Gothic novel and quickly evolves into much more. Peggy is a nurse who works in a mental asylum. If that isn't creepy enough, hold on for more. Peggy's background is extreme Bible toting, God-fearing, and even more, she is a young widow. The circumstances surrounding her husband's death are a mystery. Peggy is extremely tormented not only by her husband's death, but is haunted by outrageous nightmares. She is paranoid, scare</span>
  <span id="freeText2907728216858089437" style="display:none">The Taking of Peggy Martin by Karen Glista begins as a would be Southern Gothic novel and quickly evolves into much more. Peggy is a nurse who works in a mental asylum. If that isn't creepy enough, hold on for more. Peggy's background is extreme Bible toting, God-fearing, and even more, she is a young widow. The circumstances surrounding her husband's death are a mystery. Peggy is extremely tormented not only by her husband's death, but is haunted by outrageous nightmares. She is paranoid, scared, and on edge. Unwittingly, a horrific incident within the halls of where she works throws her further into the abyss, and we the reader watch her helplessly try to climb out. Written in the first person, which is quite effective here, Peggy becomes embroiled in something she could hardly imagine. A heady mix of gothic storytelling, the supernatural, and science fiction, this story is tough to categorize, but may keep you up at night. This story is a provocative book with an unlikely heroine.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2343269380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343269380" />
    <a title="Minion Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80003590-minion-reviews"><img alt="Minion Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522315959p2/80003590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2343269380?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Minion Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Minion Reviews" href="/user/show/80003590-minion-reviews">Minion Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343269380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15928689066744979540">This the second of two novels I’ve read by Karen, and I’ve got to say that even though I can tell it’s by the same writer, they feel entirely different. The plot in this story is unique (moreso than the other one I read), and has a lot of strength. The pace is definitely dialed back, but it’s supplemented very well with descriptive language.<br/>The details were also very realistic and accurate (much like the other novel I’ve read of hers). Karen has a knack for dialogue and character development, an</span>
  <span id="freeText15928689066744979540" style="display:none">This the second of two novels I’ve read by Karen, and I’ve got to say that even though I can tell it’s by the same writer, they feel entirely different. The plot in this story is unique (moreso than the other one I read), and has a lot of strength. The pace is definitely dialed back, but it’s supplemented very well with descriptive language.<br />The details were also very realistic and accurate (much like the other novel I’ve read of hers). Karen has a knack for dialogue and character development, and really knows how to employ visual storytelling in all of her novels. This novel, in particular, follows the tragic story of Peggy, a widowed woman who seems stuck in perpetual misfortune.<br />I’m more of a horror fan than a fantasy fan, and this book really hits the mark as a hybrid horror story; but the terror really comes from the struggle Peggy has amidst all the tragedy in her life. This is a great read, and if you like stories that can completely absorb you, then this book is for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15928689066744979540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11212851501832959023" style="display:none">The Taking of Peggy Martin is not for the faint hearted, it has violence, gore and heart-stopping scares that are sure to keep you up at night. It follows psychiatric nurse Peggy, as she grieves for her dead husband, she is convinced was murdered. Gradually losing her grip on reality, a mysterious patient causes further chaos in her world. He seems to have many strange connections to her husband's death. Furthermore, those closest to her are being picked off, one by one, by creatures not of this world. Is Peggy going insane? Or is she catching a glimpse of what awaits the world.<br /><br />It was clear that Karin Glista has done her research with this novel, which makes the plot much more believable, helping to draw you in. Reading this was like falling down the rabbit hole, but you don't end up in Wonderland, but into a dark, foreboding woods where, someone or something is determined to make sure you will never escape.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText14216601001755979946" style="display:none">Knowing nothing at all about this book, the title and front cover image intrigued me. Karen Glista immediately sets the scene and the pace is fierce and unstoppable. She uses a lot of detailed descriptions, but never to the detriment of maintaining the story’s momentum. I found it a really nail-biting read when Glista describes tense scenes, of which there are many. Glista also has a fearfully impressive vocabulary and I found myself reaching for the dictionary on more than one occasion.<br /><br />This starts out as the story of a tormented psychiatric nurse in 1950s America and as such allows great insights into life on an in-patient ward, against the backdrop of an overtly religious community. It is an epic tale, incorporating elements of mystery, psychological thriller with lashings of the supernatural. It is a real roller coaster of a read! <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText3486887162430065914" style="display:none">Glista pays lots of attention to detail in her storytelling. Her writing is precise and leaves no stone unturned, so-to-speak. She describes everything around her characters, including flora and fauna, painting vivid pictures with her words. She can even relate moments of beauty amidst a narrative of terror. This is a very believably written story set in the milieu of 1950’s America, in which Glista has carefully used a specific choice of language and dialect that add to the effect. She takes the reader on a very unusual journey, following the characters into a different, uncharted world, yet she manages to maintain the plausibility of the plot, despite entering the realms of sci-fi. If you want a novel that is unlike anything you’ve encountered before, this may well be the one for you!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2163677483" />
    <a title="Kickass Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72978914-kickass-reads"><img alt="Kickass Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528210641p2/72978914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2163677483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10489577011374852039">The Taking Of Peggy Martin is a rather unusual and ambitious story with many and varied elements to indulge in. In the first instance it’s nothing if not dramatic. It has a psychiatric hospital, incidents that are not what they seem and characters who are not what they seem. It has unflinching scenes of death and destruction, classic moments of horror, the supernatural and urban legends. It blends together religion, conspiracy, missing families, historical fiction and ultimately sci fi. It is a </span>
  <span id="freeText10489577011374852039" style="display:none">The Taking Of Peggy Martin is a rather unusual and ambitious story with many and varied elements to indulge in. In the first instance it’s nothing if not dramatic. It has a psychiatric hospital, incidents that are not what they seem and characters who are not what they seem. It has unflinching scenes of death and destruction, classic moments of horror, the supernatural and urban legends. It blends together religion, conspiracy, missing families, historical fiction and ultimately sci fi. It is a whirlwind of a story, voiced by a protagonist who undergoes just about every trauma an author can inflict on her, but without ever seeming too far fetched. As a reader, my suspension of disbelief remained intact, despite the very alien territory the story inhabits as it progresses. </span>

<div id="review_2171709619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2171709619" />
    <a title="Paragraph And A Half" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73320982-paragraph-and-a-half"><img alt="Paragraph And A Half" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526474966p2/73320982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2171709619?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paragraph And A Half" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paragraph And A Half" href="/user/show/73320982-paragraph-and-a-half">Paragraph And A Half</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2171709619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7086258325601826468">Karen Glista’s ‘The Taking of Peggy Martin’ travels through and blends more than a few genres. It starts off as a very well-written and tense horror thriller as well as being a believable piece of historical fiction, and ends as pure science fiction, grappling with the classic battle of good versus evil along the way. The main character is the ever-suffering Peggy Martin of the title. Her journey is a hellish living nightmare, beginning with insomnia and strange, unexplainable happenings at nigh</span>
  <span id="freeText7086258325601826468" style="display:none">Karen Glista’s ‘The Taking of Peggy Martin’ travels through and blends more than a few genres. It starts off as a very well-written and tense horror thriller as well as being a believable piece of historical fiction, and ends as pure science fiction, grappling with the classic battle of good versus evil along the way. The main character is the ever-suffering Peggy Martin of the title. Her journey is a hellish living nightmare, beginning with insomnia and strange, unexplainable happenings at night and culminating in a bizarre series of events of escalating terror. This book is in no way predictable or cliched, it keeps the reader intrigued, uncertain and in as much wonder as Peggy Martin herself!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7086258325601826468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

A thrilling read that drags you through the to a plot twist I would have never has saw coming. Someone please make this into a movie already.</span>

  <span id="freeText6396180125046270347" style="display:none">This is definitely one on those books that transcends genres in a successful way and I was hooked right from the beginning. I’m now planning what order to read the rest of her books in, and maybe even gifting some to friends this Christmas.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText11651488690343622945" style="display:none">I am obsessed with psychological thrillers and horrors, so when a friend recommended The Taking of Peggy Martin (which she assured me was a perfect mixture of the two), I was all over it. A dark twisting plot, an oppressive atmosphere, and a spooky institute for the criminally insane, makes for a spine-chilling novel that will have you sleeping with the lights on for a week. Steer clear of the woods. Karin Glista has written a really accomplished horror novel, that ramps up the tension right up until the shocking conclusion. She also puts in points of humor in just the right places, to diffuse some of the tension, and keep the book flowing at a manageable pace. A book I highly recommend.</span>

  <span id="freeText6003244500463882862" style="display:none">This was a quite challenging read as I felt so deeply for the Peggy Martin character. Peggy feels like a friend you want to put your arm around and protect, but are helpless to prevent the things happening while eagerly reading on and hoping she will be ok. I think maybe because of the heightened jeopardy and empathy for Peggy I found I couldn’t put the book down, and trying to I just couldn’t switch off from the story and went back to it immediately. That has to be the mark of a very good book, though, when it sits with you and you can’t shake from your thoughts. All in all a fantastic read, and I think one I’ll be rereading in the future.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hgq4/6iMd1Oejvns2eULg68Xrrx0yfDJPv407fCXJ6651CvCV7lUHvzoEY4mngBa7SXuHp5D0dHwQGyWr5YONg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y0valPXOsFDflr+IeTla4w23a0PFlwGm+QDDb2k3rmhclUmpCvuTHb3wV+qGQlE6T4Ur4S8dIL43vpsUNjaH8A==')})
  }
